## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor rate laws / dynamical systems for concentration)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard form of a kinetic rate law for a (batch) chemical species. With only t and A available, the most likely governing relations are mass-action-type ODEs, possibly with time-varying effective rate coefficients or approach-to-equilibrium/source terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition, pseudo-first-order)
- Second-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or A + A -> products)
- n-th order (power-law) rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order or lumped mechanism)
- Source + first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous generation with linear removal; well-mixed with feed/decay)
- Relaxation to equilibrium concentration: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady/equilibrium level A_eq = c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-like kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-accelerating at low A with limiting depletion or inhibition at high A)
- Saturating/inhibited rate (rational form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by saturation/inhibition; transitions from ~-A to ~constant)
- Time-varying first-order rate (deactivating catalyst or changing conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective k(t) decreases with time)
- Time-varying first-order rate (activation/warm-up): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective k(t) increases with time)
- Induction/turn-on kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) (reaction starts slowly then approaches a steady effective rate)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., modulated irradiation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) (time-periodic effective rate coefficient)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action order identification: polynomial/power dependence of dA_dt on A (A, A**2, A**n) indicates elementary or lumped reaction order.
- Presence of a nonzero intercept at A = 0: dA_dt = c0 - c1*A suggests a source term (generation, inflow, or back-reaction from an unmodeled reservoir).
- Approach-to-equilibrium signature: dependence on (A - c1) indicates relaxation toward an equilibrium/steady concentration A_eq.
- Autocatalysis vs inhibition: a positive linear term in A with a negative quadratic term (c0*A - c1*A**2) implies self-acceleration at low A with limiting effects at higher A.
- Saturation/inhibition mechanisms: rational forms like A/(A + c1) imply a transition between low-A proportionality and high-A rate-limiting behavior.
- Time-dependent effective rate constants: multiplicative factors of t (e.g., exp(-c*t), 1/(1+exp(-c*t)), sin(c*t)) indicate changing operating conditions, catalyst deactivation/activation, or external driving.
- Finite-time switching/induction periods: sigmoidal functions of t multiplying A indicate delayed onset due to mixing, heating, inhibitor consumption, or catalyst activation.
- Stoichiometric constraints: if A must remain nonnegative, plausible learned structures often satisfy dA_dt -> 0 as A -> 0 (e.g., proportional-to-A forms) unless an explicit source term is present.
